A cartographic depiction of the current situation in Mosul, as of January 25, 2017. <span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#EDC4BE solid 1px;; background-color:#EDC4BE; color:#EDC4BE">    </span> Iraqi Government control</span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#B4B2AE solid 1px;; background-color:#B4B2AE; color:#B4B2AE">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIL</a> control</span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#FFFF00 solid 1px;; background-color:#FFFF00; color:#FFFF00">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a> control</span></td>

<td>Ongoing</td>

<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Territorial<br/>
changes</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>ISF completely capture eastern Mosul by 24 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of 3 December 2016, ISF and Peshmerga have captured a total of 5,677 square kilometres (2,192 sq mi) and 369 villages from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq"><img alt="Iraq" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="274" data-file-width="411" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Iraq.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iraq.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Iraq.svg/35px-Flag_of_Iraq.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Iraq.svg/45px-Flag_of_Iraq.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> 54,000–60,000 ISF troops<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1017_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1017-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ptv-31">[31]</a></sup><br/>
14,000 paramilitary troops<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1017_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1017-30">[30]</a></sup><br/>
<span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan"><img alt="Iraqi Kurdistan" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Kurdistan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> 40,000 Peshmerga troops<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1017_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1017-30">[30]</a></sup><br/>
<b>Total:</b> 108,500–114,000 fighters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mosul_battle_forces_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mosul_battle_forces-32">[32]</a></sup><br/></p>
<b>Support:</b><br/>
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="415" height="25" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg/25px-Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg/38px-Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg/50px-Seal_of_Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve.svg.png 2x" title="no" width="25"/></span> Hundreds of CJTF–OIR personnel</td>

<li><b><a href="/wiki/Iranian_intervention_in_Iraq_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Iranian intervention in Iraq (2014–present)">Iranian-led intervention</a></b></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/American-led_intervention_in_Iraq_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="American-led intervention in Iraq (2014–present)">American-led intervention</a></b>

<p><b>ISIL executions</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mass_executions_in_ISIL_occupied_Mosul" title="Mass executions in ISIL occupied Mosul">Mosul</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Battle of Mosul</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">معركة الموصل</span>‎‎; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Kurdish_language" title="Central Kurdish language">Central Kurdish</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ckb" xml:lang="ckb">شەڕی مووسڵ</span>‎) is a joint offensive by Iraqi government forces with allied militias, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">Iraqi Kurdistan</a>, and international forces to retake the city of <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> (ISIL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The offensive, dubbed Operation "<b>We Are Coming, Nineveh</b>" (<span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">قادمون يا نينوى</span>; <i>Qadimun Ya Naynawa</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlantic1020_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic1020-49">[49]</a></sup> began on 16 October 2016, with forces besieging ISIL-controlled areas in the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Governorate" title="Nineveh Governorate">Nineveh Governorate</a> surrounding Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibt1016_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibt1016-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1017_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1017-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1016_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1016-52">[52]</a></sup> The battle for <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a> is considered key in the <a href="/wiki/Military_intervention_against_ISIL" title="Military intervention against ISIL">military intervention against ISIL</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Mosul" title="Fall of Mosul">seized the city</a> in June 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Outnumbering <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIL</a> forces 10 to 1, it is the largest deployment of Iraqi troops since the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt1017_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-dt1017-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The operation follows the <a href="/wiki/Mosul_offensive_(2015)" title="Mosul offensive (2015)">Mosul offensives in 2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mosul_offensive_(2016)" title="Mosul offensive (2016)">2016</a>. The offensive began with Iraqi troops and <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a> fighters engaging ISIL on three fronts outside Mosul, going from village to village in the surrounding area. More than 120 towns and villages were liberated from ISIL control in the first two weeks of fighting. At dawn on 1 November, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Special_Operations_Forces" title="Iraqi Special Operations Forces">Iraqi Special Operations Forces</a> entered the city on the eastern front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rferl1101_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-rferl1101-55">[55]</a></sup> Meeting with fierce fighting, the Iraqi advance into the city was slowed by elaborate defenses – including road blocks, booby traps, suicide bombers and snipers – and by the presence of civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Battle of Mosul is concurrent with the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_al-Bab" title="Battle of al-Bab">Battle of al-Bab</a> by the Turkish-led FSA forces, and the <a href="/wiki/Raqqa_offensive_(2016%E2%80%93present)" title="Raqqa offensive (2016–present)">Raqqa offensive</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Democratic_Forces" title="Syrian Democratic Forces">Syrian Democratic Forces</a> (SDF) on ISIL's capital city and stronghold in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016.08_Mosul_area.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1015" data-file-width="1828" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/2016.08_Mosul_area.svg/300px-2016.08_Mosul_area.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/2016.08_Mosul_area.svg/450px-2016.08_Mosul_area.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/2016.08_Mosul_area.svg/600px-2016.08_Mosul_area.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016.08_Mosul_area.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the territorial control during the 2016 Mosul offensive, as of August 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_background">General background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: General background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Mosul" title="Fall of Mosul">Fall of Mosul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mosul_offensive_(2015)" title="Mosul offensive (2015)">Mosul offensive (2015)</a></div>
<p>Mosul is Iraq's second most populous city. It <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Mosul" title="Fall of Mosul">fell</a> to 800 ISIL militants in June 2014, because of the largely <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> population's deep distrust of the primarily <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shia</a> Iraqi government and its corrupt armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lemonde1017_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-lemonde1017-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1016_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1016-58">[58]</a></sup> It was in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_al-Nuri_(Mosul)" title="Great Mosque of al-Nuri (Mosul)">Great Mosque in Mosul</a> that ISIL leader <a href="/wiki/Abu_Bakr_al-Baghdadi" title="Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi">Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi</a> declared the beginning of ISIL's self-proclaimed "caliphate" which spans Iraq and Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1016_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1016-58">[58]</a></sup> The original population of 2.5 million has fallen to approximately 1.5 million after two years of ISIL rule. The city was once extremely diverse, with ethnic minorities including <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Iraq" title="Armenians in Iraq">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen" title="Iraqi Turkmen">Turkmen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shabak_people" title="Shabak people">Shabak</a> people, all of whom have suffered and continue to suffer considerably under the (majority Sunni Arab) Islamic State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Mosul remains the last stronghold of ISIL in Iraq,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt1017_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1017-60">[60]</a></sup> and the anticipated offensive to reclaim it was hyped as the "mother of all battles".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations_for_the_battle">Preparations for the battle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Preparations for the battle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mosul_offensive_(2016)" title="Mosul offensive (2016)">Mosul offensive (2016)</a></div>
<p>In the weeks leading up to the ground offensive, the US-led <a href="/wiki/Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve" title="Combined Joint Task Force – Operation Inherent Resolve">CJTF - OIR</a> coalition bombed ISIL targets, and the Iraqi Army made gradual advances on the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt1017_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-dt1017-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>'s <a href="/wiki/General_Atomics_MQ-9_Reaper" title="General Atomics MQ-9 Reaper">Reaper</a> drones, <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Typhoons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado" title="Panavia Tornado">Tornados</a> targeted "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocket_launchers" title="Rocket launchers">rocket launchers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> <a href="/wiki/Stockpile_(military)" title="Stockpile (military)">stockpiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> pieces and <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> positions" in the 72 hours before the ground assault began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Airborne_leaflet_propaganda" title="Airborne leaflet propaganda">Leaflets</a> dropped on the city by the Iraqi army advised young male residents to "rise up" against ISIL when the battle began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt1017_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1017-60">[60]</a></sup> To prepare defenses against the assault, ISIL operatives dug 4 m<sup>2</sup> holes around the city, which they planned to fill with burning oil to reduce visibility<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt1017_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-dt1017-54">[54]</a></sup> and slow advances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-ptv-31">[31]</a></sup> They also built hundreds of elaborate tunnels in the villages surrounding Mosul, rigged with explosives and booby-traps, and laid <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised explosive devices</a> (IEDs) and mines along the roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> There was considerable concern that ISIL may employ chemical weapons against soldiers and civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj1030_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-aj1030-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Iraqi sources, the assault towards Mosul was being waged from Al-Khazer axis (east of Mosul), <a href="/wiki/Mosul_Dam" title="Mosul Dam">Mosul Dam</a> (northern axis), <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Baashiqa</a> axis (eastern axis), Al-Qayyarah axis (southern axis), and Talul el-Baj- Al-Khadr axis (southwestern axis).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forces_involved_in_the_offensive">Forces involved in the offensive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Forces involved in the offensive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1356" data-file-width="2048" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg/300px-Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg/450px-Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg/600px-Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lt._Gen._Stephen_J._Townsend_Qayyarah_September_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Lt. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_J._Townsend" title="Stephen J. Townsend">Stephen J. Townsend</a>, commander of the Combined Joint Task Force, at <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah_Airfield_West" title="Qayyarah Airfield West">Qayyarah Airfield West</a>, 22 September 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>About 3,000–5,000 ISIL fighters were estimated to be in Mosul city, according to the United States Department of Defense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Other estimates ranged as low as 2,000 and high as 12,000 ISIL fighters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lemonde1017_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-lemonde1017-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-35">[35]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i> estimated approximately 8,000–9,000 fighters loyal to ISIL, with "[h]alf of them... highly trained, and the rest... either teenagers or not well trained. About ten percent of the fighters are foreign (Arabs and non-Arabs). The rest are Iraqis. Most are from Nineveh’s townships and districts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Iraqi-led coalition was initially estimated by <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> to have 94,000 members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> but this number was later revised upward to 108,500;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mosul_battle_forces_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mosul_battle_forces-32">[32]</a></sup> 54,000 to 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_security_forces" title="Iraqi security forces">Iraqi security forces</a> (ISF) soldiers, 16,000 <a href="/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces" title="Popular Mobilization Forces">Popular Mobilization Forces</a> (PMF) fighters, and 40,000 <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a> (including approximately 200 Iranian Kurdish female fighters from <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Freedom_Party" title="Kurdistan Freedom Party">PAK</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> are deployed in the battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1017_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1017-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-ptv-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the PMF units, the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Plain_Protection_Units" title="Nineveh Plain Protection Units">Nineveh Plain Protection Units</a> composed of <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a> are among the paramilitary forces in the Iraqi coalition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPF_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPF-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Shia militias including several brigades of the paramilitary organization Hashd al-Shaabi, the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Companies" title="Peace Companies">Peace Companies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kata%27ib_Hezbollah" title="Kata'ib Hezbollah">Kata'ib Hezbollah</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_of_the_Righteous" title="League of the Righteous">League of the Righteous</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Badr_Organization" title="Badr Organization">Badr Organization</a>, Saraya Ashura, Saraya Khorasani, <a href="/wiki/Kata%27ib_al-Imam_Ali" title="Kata'ib al-Imam Ali">Kata'ib al-Imam Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harakat_Hezbollah_al-Nujaba" title="Harakat Hezbollah al-Nujaba">Harakat Hezbollah al-Nujaba</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkmen_Brigades_(PMU)" title="Turkmen Brigades (PMU)">Turkmen Brigades</a> also took part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMF_cut_off_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-PMF_cut_off-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lobs1017_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-lobs1017-76">[76]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ezidi" title="Ezidi">Ezidi</a> community of the Sinjar region contributes <a href="/wiki/Sinjar_Resistance_Units" title="Sinjar Resistance Units">Sinjar Resistance Units</a> (YBŞ) and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Az%C3%AEdxan_Women%27s_Units" title="Êzîdxan Women's Units">Êzîdxan Women's Units</a> (YJÊ),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ezidi_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ezidi-77">[77]</a></sup> which are operating in concert with Sunni Arab <a href="/wiki/Shammar" title="Shammar">Shammar</a> tribal militias and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Defence_Forces" title="People's Defence Forces">People's Defence Forces</a> (HPG) of the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers' Party">Kurdistan Workers' Party</a> (PKK).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrian</a> forces involved in the planned offensive includes the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Plain_Forces" title="Nineveh Plain Forces">NPF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwekh_Nawsha" title="Dwekh Nawsha">Dwekh Nawsha</a> who both are allied alongside Kurdish <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil,_Iraq.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg/250px-Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg/375px-Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg/500px-Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil%2C_Iraq.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peshmerga_soldiers_prepare_to_conduct_a_combined_arms_live-fire_exercise_near_Erbil,_Iraq.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a> soldiers prepare to conduct a combined arms live-fire exercise with an Italian instructor near <a href="/wiki/Erbil" title="Erbil">Erbil</a>, on 12 October 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Operation_Inherent_Resolve" title="Combined Joint Task Force – Operation Inherent Resolve">international coalition</a> of 60 nations, led by the United States, is supporting Iraq's war against ISIL, providing logistical and air support, intelligence, and advice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The international coalition forces are headquartered 60 kilometres (37 mi) south of Mosul at <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah_Airfield_West" title="Qayyarah Airfield West">Qayyarah Airfield West</a> (or Q-West) in <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah" title="Qayyarah">Qayyarah</a>, which was reclaimed from ISIL in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> About 560 U.S. troops from the <a href="/wiki/101st_Airborne_Division" title="101st Airborne Division">101st Airborne Division</a> were deployed to Q-West for the battle, including command and control elements, a security detachment, an airfield operations team, and logistics and communications specialists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The U.S. deployed <a href="/wiki/HIMARS" title="HIMARS">HIMARS</a> rocket launchers and <a href="/wiki/M777_howitzer" title="M777 howitzer">M777 howitzers</a>, manned by the 101st's 2nd Brigade Combat Team and the Golf Company, 526th Brigade Support Battalion. The French army deployed four <a href="/wiki/CAESAR_self-propelled_howitzer" title="CAESAR self-propelled howitzer">CAESAR</a> howitzers and 150 to 200 soldiers at Qayyarah, with 600 more French troops announced at the end of September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> An additional 150 French soldiers are in <a href="/wiki/Erbil" title="Erbil">Erbil</a>, east of Mosul, training Peshmerga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lobs1017_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-lobs1017-76">[76]</a></sup> The aircraft carrier <i><a href="/wiki/French_aircraft_carrier_Charles_de_Gaulle" title="French aircraft carrier Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a></i>, with a squadron of 24 <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Rafale M jets</a>, was deployed from <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a> to the Syrian coast to support the operation against ISIL through airstrikes and reconnaissance missions; 12 other Rafale jets are operating out of French Air Force bases in Jordan and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnncdg_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnncdg-86">[86]</a></sup> 80 Australian special forces soldiers and 210 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Special_Operations_Forces_Command" title="Canadian Special Operations Forces Command">CANSOFCOM</a> soldiers were also deployed to assist the Peshmerga. In addition, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> <a href="/wiki/21_Electronic_Warfare_Regiment" title="21 Electronic Warfare Regiment">21 Electronic Warfare Regiment</a> was also reported to be in the area, working to intercept and relay ISIL communications, while a Role 2 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces_Health_Services_Group" title="Canadian Forces Health Services Group">Canadian Army field hospital</a> with 60 personnel has been set up to treat Kurdish casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okra_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Okra-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CANSOFCOM_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-CANSOFCOM-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical,_biological,_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3362" data-file-width="5044" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg/300px-An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg/450px-An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg/600px-An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical%2C_biological%2C_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:An_Iraqi_soldier_attending_a_course_on_chemical,_biological,_radiological_and_nuclear_defense_training_at_Camp_Taji.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Iraqi soldier during a course on chemical, biological, radiological and nuclear defense training at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Taji" title="Camp Taji">Camp Taji</a>. Coalition forces have expressed fears ISIL may use chemical weapons during the Battle of Mosul.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Iraq_Region" title="Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party – Iraq Region">Ba'ath loyalists</a> group, known to be led by <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>'s former vice president <a href="/wiki/Izzat_Ibrahim_al-Douri" title="Izzat Ibrahim al-Douri">Izzat Ibrahim al-Douri</a>, issued a statement before the start of operations calling for the people of the city to start an uprising against ISIL and announced that they will fight the "terrorist organization."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naqshabandi_-_Bawwabat_Al-Arab_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Naqshabandi_-_Bawwabat_Al-Arab-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naqshabandi_-_Azzaman_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Naqshabandi_-_Azzaman-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_the_battle">Timeline of the battle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Timeline of the battle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

(<a href="/wiki/Talk:Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)#Split_proposed_-_Timeline_of_the_Battle_of_Mosul" title="Talk:Battle of Mosul (2016–17)">Discuss</a>) <small><i>(November 2016)</i></small></span></td>

</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="October_2016:_Initial_advances">October 2016: Initial advances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: October 2016: Initial advances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl>
<dt>16–17 October</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg/300px-M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg/450px-M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg/600px-M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M109A6_Paladin_at_Qayyarah_October_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A U.S. Army <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M109A6_Paladin" title="M109A6 Paladin">M109A6 Paladin</a> conducts a fire mission at <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah_Airfield_West" title="Qayyarah Airfield West">Qayyarah Airfield West</a>, in support of the Iraqi security forces' push toward Mosul, 17 October 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 16 October, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">Haider al-Abadi</a> declared the beginning of the assault to recapture the city of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1016_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1016-52">[52]</a></sup> Officials reported howitzers firing on ISIL targets later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibt1016_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibt1016-50">[50]</a></sup> The main assault began on 17 October at approximately 6 a.m.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt1017_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1017-60">[60]</a></sup> with shelling and arrival of armored vehicles to the front lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The Peshmerga in the Khazir region east of Mosul started the ground assault by advancing on ISIL-held villages from three fronts, with Iraqi security forces advancing from the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Iraqi troops advanced on the <a href="/wiki/Bartella" title="Bartella">Bartella</a> area east of Mosul while ISIL fighters fired mortars at Peshmerga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj1017_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1017-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="President of Iraqi Kurdistan">President of Iraqi Kurdistan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Massoud_Barzani" title="Massoud Barzani">Massoud Barzani</a>, said that Peshmerga and Iraqi fighters retook 200 square kilometers (80 square miles) from ISIL on the first day of fighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj1017_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-aj1017-94">[94]</a></sup> Iraqi officials reported that "heavy losses of life and equipment" were inflicted upon ISIL fighters in the Hamdaniya district southeast of Mosul. ISIL fighters who were wounded in the battle were reported to have been bused towards the group's Syrian headquarters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raqqa" title="Raqqa">Raqqa</a> for medical aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1017_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1017-30">[30]</a></sup> The anti-ISIL coalition destroyed 52 targets during the day<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-straightstimes_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-straightstimes-95">[95]</a></sup> Family members of ISIL fighters fled from Mosul to the village of Nawran due to the shelling. It was also reported that some fighters had started shaving their beards and were getting rid of their Afghan uniforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The group was also reported to have evacuated and shifted its headquarters from west side of Mosul to its east side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> A bridge into Mosul known as the "Freedom Bridge" was destroyed on 17 October. Peshmerga sources blamed ISIL for its destruction, while ISIL claimed it was blown up by airstrikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>18 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 18 October, The Iraqi government declared that 20 villages near Mosul were captured from ISIL in the first 24 hours of fighting by the Peshmerga and Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> On the southern front, Iraqi troops retook several villages near <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah" title="Qayyarah">Qayyarah</a>, including al-Sirt, Bajwaniya, al-Hud and al-Mashraf, and parts of the al-Hamdaniya District southeast of Mosul. Iraqi Federal Police also regained control of 56 oilfields in the Qayyarah district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> According to reports, the Peshmerga were met with little resistance on the eastern front, while Iraqi and PMF fighters coming from the south were facing tougher resistance from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian1018_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1018-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coalition strategy was reported to be encircling Mosul completely before Iraqi troops advanced into the city-center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcnews1018_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews1018-102">[102]</a></sup> Early in the day on 18 October, Iraqi forces in the east came close to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qaraqosh" title="Qaraqosh">Qaraqosh</a> (Bakhdida), once the largest Assyrian town in Iraq, and fighters in the south were closing in on Hammam al-'Alil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-straightstimes_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-straightstimes-95">[95]</a></sup> Iraqi Army later stormed Qaraqosh and fought with ISIL fighters who remained holed up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1018_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1018-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The Iraqi and Peshmerga advance had been slowed down during the same day due to suicide bombers, roadside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_devices" title="Improvised explosive devices">IEDs</a> and oil fires. In order to eliminate any ISIL presence completely from the villages on the outskirts of the city, they were carrying out street-by-street search operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The Peshmerga later paused their advance while the Iraqi Army continued its advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1280" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg/300px-Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg/450px-Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg/600px-Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_-_Iraqi_security_forces_transport_combat_equipment_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Iraqi security forces transport combat equipment including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M1A1_Abrams" title="M1A1 Abrams">M1A1 Abrams</a> tanks and <a href="/wiki/BMP-1" title="BMP-1">BMP-1</a> infantry fighting vehicles to tactical assembly areas with assistance from the 313th Movement Control Battalion forward element, on 18 October 2016, near Makhmur, Iraq</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pro-government fighters in the south of Mosul were battling pockets of ISIL fighters and snipers as they tried to reclaim the village of Abbasi,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and expected to soon take control of the village of Zawiya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Fighting resumed in the village of Kani Harami, which was captured by the Iraqi Army a day earlier but recaptured by ISIL on 18 October as the Army lacked reinforcements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1018_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1018-104">[104]</a></sup> The Army also retook the village of Al-Hud on the Tigris, where villagers had risen up against ISIL and killed at least 9 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> State police also secured the <a href="/wiki/Al-Mishraq" title="Al-Mishraq">Al-Mishraq</a> sulfur plant south of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The al-Shura district was stated by its mayor to have been captured by the Iraqi security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Joint airstrikes by Iraqi and coalition warplanes on ISIL headquarters in Mosul destroyed 13 targets and killed 35 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the Iraqi Army advanced on Mosul, rebellion against ISIL broke out in the city. The group's Islamic Police revolted and attacked four headquarters of the organisation. The revolt was put down with 7 rebellious leaders being killed and many militants being executed. A group of rebels attacked a headquarters of the group the next day, killed 2 militants and raised the Iraqi flag over the building. ISIL patrols in the city were also attacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>A group of <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Men_of_the_Naqshbandi_Order" title="Army of the Men of the Naqshbandi Order">Naqshabandi Army</a> militants reportedly attacked an ISIL controlled checkpoint in the village of Al-Houd, wounding two ISIL militants before they were captured along with a few other militants who attacked a group of ISIL militants in the same village in coordination with the PMF on the day before. In total, 30 Naqshabandi militants were captured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>19 October</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4468" data-file-width="6255" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg/300px-Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg/450px-Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg/600px-Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Airmen_prepare_to_load_a_Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Airmen assigned to the <a href="/wiki/379th_Air_Expeditionary_Wing" title="379th Air Expeditionary Wing">379th Expeditionary Aircraft Maintenance Squadron</a> prepare to load a <a href="/wiki/Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition" title="Joint Direct Attack Munition">Joint Direct Attack Munition</a> onto an aircraft on 19 October as part of the U.S.-led airstrikes supporting the offensive.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Iraqi army resumed fighting on 19 October, surrounding Qaraqosh with ISIL deploying snipers and car bombs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Lt. Gen. Qassim al-Maliki declared that Iraqi forces had captured 13 villages north and northeast of Al Quwayr, south of Mosul. The Iraqi Army was also reported to be within 6 kilometres (3.7 mi) from the outskirts of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The village of Kani Harami was captured after heavy fighting in the morning with the militants retreating to Abbasiyah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1019_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1019-123">[123]</a></sup> A total of 22 towns were reported to have been captured, with 12 by the Peshmerga and 10 by the ISF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Nofal Hammadi, governor of the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Governorate" title="Nineveh Governorate">Nineveh Governorate</a>, declared that 40% of the province had been retaken from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The offensive to retake the town of <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a> northeast of Mosul, originally scheduled for dawn, was delayed due to lack of logistical support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Thousands of Peshmerga were reportedly preparing to retake Bashiqa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The international coalition's commander Gary Voelsky also stated that a majority of ISIL leaders were fleeing Mosul and predicted foreign fighters will form the majority of militants remaining in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian1020_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian1020-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>20 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>The fighting grew more intense on 20 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1020_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1020-130">[130]</a></sup> A large convoy of <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Special_Operations_Forces" title="Iraqi Special Operations Forces">Golden Division</a> arrived at positions retaken by the Peshmerga forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> They also captured <a href="/wiki/Bartella" title="Bartella">Bartella</a>. ISIL fighters detonated 9 truck bombs during the fighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> According to Maj. Gen. Maan al-Saadi of the Iraqi Army, 200 ISIL fighters were killed in the fight for Bartella.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1020_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1020-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Peshmerga and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/NPF" title="NPF">NPF</a> also announced a "large-scale operation" to the north and northeast of Mosul, aiming to retake the Assyrian towns of <a href="/wiki/Tesqopa" title="Tesqopa">Tesqopa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian1020_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian1020-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> During the day, the Peshmerga liberated 6 villages, including 4 on the Bashiqa front line and 2 on the Nawaran front. In addition, they also entered another 4 villages. They briefly captured the village of Tiz Khirab but were forced to withdraw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1020_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1020-134">[134]</a></sup> On the southern front, Iraqi forces resumed their push north after a brief pause<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj1020_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1020-135">[135]</a></sup> and recaptured six villages east of <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah" title="Qayyarah">Qayyarah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1020_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1020-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>A U.S. bomb disposal expert embedded with the Peshmerga was killed after the vehicle he was riding in drove over a roadside bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> ISIL also set Al-Mishraq sulfur plant on fire, causing two deaths and nearly 1,000 hospitalizations from sulfur fume inhalation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> An ISIL ambush near Bashiqa left dozens of Peshmerga dead or wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj1020_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1020-135">[135]</a></sup> The group was also reported to be digging trenches to slow the advancement of coalition troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>21 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>ISIL launched multiple attacks in <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">Kirkuk</a> on 21 October to divert military resources. Multiple explosions on the southern front, Iraqi troops retook several villages near <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah" title="Qayyarah">Qayyarah</a>, including al-Sirt, Bajwaniya, al-Hud and al-Mashraf, and parts of the al-Hamdaniya District southeast of Mosul. Iraqi Federal Police also regained control of 56 oilfields in the Qayyarah district.ns and gun battles in the city, mostly centered on a government compound were reported. A suicide bomber killed 13 workers, including four Iranians, at a power plant in <a href="/wiki/Dibis_District" title="Dibis District">Dibis</a>. A senior Peshmerga commander said that attackers had entered by posing as <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">IDPs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Iraqi government forces meanwhile reported that they had retaken 2 more villages south of Mosul and killed 15 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>22 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 22 October, Iraqi police declared that ISIL's attack on Kirkuk had been repelled and all attackers had been killed or had blown themselves up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1022_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc1022-141">[141]</a></sup> Iraqi officials also stated that 80 people were killed in Kirkuk, primarily Kurdish security forces, and about 170 wounded; 56 ISIL militants were also killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> A reporter of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmeneli_TV" title="Türkmeneli TV">Türkmeneli TV</a> also died in the attack,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1022_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-abc1022-141">[141]</a></sup> while at least seven journalists were wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>A large-scale offensive began to retake the Assyrian town of <a href="/wiki/Bakhdida" title="Bakhdida">Qaraqosh</a> which remained under ISIL control after several days of fighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Iraqi troops also advanced on the town of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Keppe" title="Tel Keppe">Tel Keppe</a>, north of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1022_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1022-145">[145]</a></sup> Shifting winds sent the gas from the ablaze Al Mishraq sulphur plant to <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah_Airfield_West" title="Qayyarah Airfield West">Qayyarah Airfield West</a>, where U.S. and coalition forces were forced to use gas masks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1022_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-abc1022-141">[141]</a></sup> A journalist was also killed by a sniper in the al-Shura area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1022_141-3"><a href="#cite_note-abc1022-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i> reported that ISIL had executed detainees and teens aged 15–18 comprised the majority of ISIL fighters in Mosul. The group was also reported to have planted bombs and booby traps throughout the city and was preparing for battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>23–24 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Peshmerga claimed on 23 October that they had recaptured <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aus_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-aus-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> however it was reported on the following day that they were still trying to capture it with the help of Turkish military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The Peshmerga General Command also stated that Peshmerge had cordoned off 8 villages and had secured a significant stretch of the Bashiqa-Mosul highway. It also stated that they were now within 9 kilometres (5.6 mi) of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>ISIL increased its counterattacks in order to distract the pro-government advancing towards Mosul. In addition to the attack on Kirkuk on 21 October, ISIL fighters struck <a href="/wiki/Ar-Rutbah" title="Ar-Rutbah">Ar-Rutbah</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Sinjar" title="Sinjar">Sinjar</a>. Yazidi provincial chief Mahma Xelil said that at least 15 ISIL fighters were killed and two Peshmerga wounded in a two-hour battle in Sinjar. ISIL claimed its forces destroyed two Peshmerga vehicles, killing all on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1024_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1024-151">[151]</a></sup> Nearly 800 ISIL fighters had been killed while 78 villages were reported to have been retaken from the group as of 24 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The attack on Kirkuk was also brought to an end by 24 October, with 74 militants being killed and others including the leader of the attackers being arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>25 October</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg/220px-US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg/330px-US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg/440px-US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_and_Iraqi_leaders_discuss_battle_plans_at_Q-West.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Army and Iraqi military leaders discuss battle plans at Qayyarah Airfield West, 25 October.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Iraqi Special Operations Forces, advancing on Mosul from the east of the city, were reported to be within 2 kilometres (1.2 mi) of the city and were pausing to wait for reinforcements before proceeding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1025_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1025-154">[154]</a></sup> Turkish military supporting the Peshmerga destroyed several ISIL targets in the Bashiqa region of Northern Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> ISIL also used the burning oil trenches to impede the visibility of the Iraqi Air Force and international coalition air force and executed 9 deserters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>26 October</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1986" data-file-width="2984" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg/300px-Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg/450px-Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg/600px-Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafale_receives_fuel_from_a_KC-10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A French <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Dassault Rafale</a> is refueled from a <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_KC-10_Extender" title="McDonnell Douglas KC-10 Extender">KC-10 Extender</a> on 26 October near Iraq. The French Air Force has 24 Rafale-Ms supporting the coalition forces.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Iraqi forces were met with heavy resistance from ISIL as they attempted to clear the militants from villages in Shora, south of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1026_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1026-158">[158]</a></sup> Hundreds of ISIL suicide bombers were reported to have been sent from Syria to defend Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1026_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1026-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Peshmerga forces captured the village of Derk, 12 kilometres (7.5 mi) northeast of Mosul, where they discovered a large ISIL tunnel containing a large cache of weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1026_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1026-160">[160]</a></sup> Stephen Townsend, the commander of US forces in Iraq, stated that coalition forces had delivered more than 2,100 aerial bombs, artillery and mortar shells, rockets and missiles since the offensive to retake Mosul started. The Iraqi government stated that that 57 Iraqi soldiers had been killed and about 250 wounded while 20 to 30 Peshmerga fighters are thought to have been killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1027_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1027-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>27 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>Captain Fahd al-Laithi of Iraq's National Information Agency stated that 13 militants were killed in a coalition airstrike that targeted an IS concentration in the <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a> district while Iraqi forces had managed to retake 2 villages to the south of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The head of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Central_Command" title="United States Central Command">United States Central Command</a>, Gen. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Votel" title="Joseph Votel">Joseph Votel</a> stated that 800-900 militants had been killed in the battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1027_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1027-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>28 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>U.S. military officials estimated on 28 October that were 3,000 to 5,000 ISIL fighters left defending Mosul while 1,500 to 2,000 militants were stationed outside the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Abdulrahman al Wagga, a member of Nineveh provincial council, stated that Iraqi forces had retaken the town of Al-Shura, to the south of Mosul and had evacuated 5,000 to 6,000 civilians from there. He further stated that the area was now being cleared of homemade bombs and booby traps while security forces had almost surrounded Hammam al-Alil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1028_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1028-164">[164]</a></sup> He also stated Iraqi security forces might storm Hammam al-Alil in the next few hours but that it would depend on the situation on the ground, as civilians were still present and ISIL militants were using a "scorched earth" policy by destroying houses, buildings and bridges to slow them down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Peshmerga and Iraqi forces also captured Fadiliya, which lies just 4 km away from Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> UN meanwhile stated that ISIL had taken tens of thousands of civilians to use as human shields in Mosul, including at least 5,000 families from around Al-Shura and 2,210 families from the Nimrud area of Hamdaniya. Those who refused to go were executed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1028_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1028-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>29 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>The PMF stated on 29 October they had launched an offensive towards the west of Mosul with an aim to capture villages west of Mosul and reach the town of <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a> in order to prevent ISIL fighters from retreating into neighboring Syria or any reinforcement for their defense of Mosul. They have been tasked with recapturing around 14,000 km<sup>2</sup> of territory from the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1029_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1029-170">[170]</a></sup> They also stated that they would not enter Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Iraqi Army and PMF captured 15 villages from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1029_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1029-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i> confirmed that civilians from outside Mosul had been abducted and forced into the city by ISIL which was confiscating homes from people for their own use. A new escape route from Mosul had been set up by Syrian Kurds, who were charging $3,000 per person to smuggle people out of the city to Turkey. The blog also reported that all bridges into the city were booby-trapped with IEDs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>30 October</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Peshmerga stated on 30 October that they had captured six more villages to north and east of Mosul, and had seized control of several major roads and landmarks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> It also stated that it had captured 500 square kilometers of territory since the operation began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> PMF meanwhile stated that they had captured eight more villages to the southwest of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Observatory_for_Human_Rights" title="Syrian Observatory for Human Rights">SOHR</a> stated that at least 480 Syrian fighters including 300 child soldiers (known as "Cubs of the Caliphate") brought to Iraq by ISIL had been killed since the offensive began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudawchild_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudawchild-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>31 October</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg/300px-U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg/450px-U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg/600px-U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Soldier_prepares_for_key_leader_engagement_to_assess_Iraqi_security_force_checkpoints_at_Q-West.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A U.S. soldier of the <a href="/wiki/101st_Airborne_Division" title="101st Airborne Division">101st Airborne Division</a> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Special_Operations_Forces" title="Iraqi Special Operations Forces">Iraqi Special Operations Forces</a> discuss assessment of Iraqi security force checkpoints on 31 October at <a href="/wiki/Qayyarah_Airfield_West" title="Qayyarah Airfield West">Qayyarah Airfield West</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 31 October, a major Iraqi operation was launched on Bazwaya, to the east of Mosul. The ISOF came under heavy fire from ISIL but managed to capture the town along with several nearby villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> After capturing Bazwaya, ISOF were less than 1 mile (1.6 km) from Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1031_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc1031-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several Iraqi military officials stated that ISOF will begin its push into Mosul shortly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The U.S.-led coalition meanwhile aimed to target ISIL militants from the air if they attempted to flee the city. The US Department of Defense stated that hundreds of militants were believed to have already escaped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Iraqi Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">Haider al-Abadi</a> meanwhile called on ISIL fighters in Mosul to surrender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc1031_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-abc1031-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="November:_Entering_East_Mosul.2C_reaching_Tal_Afar">November: Entering East Mosul, reaching Tal Afar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: November: Entering East Mosul, reaching Tal Afar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl>
<dt>1 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>The operation to enter the city began at dawn on 1 November. The forces began their assault in Mosul's eastern Karama district, with artillery, tank and machine-gun fire on ISIL positions as they prepared the larger push into the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Airstrikes by the U.S.-led coalition were targeting ISIL positions, and ISIL had started tire fires to reduce visibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rferl1101_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-rferl1101-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heavy fighting occurred in the Gogjali district, at the gate of the entrance to eastern Mosul, where ISIL militants used car bombs and sniper fire to try to halt the advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1101_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1101-184">[184]</a></sup> The Golden Division entered Mosul's city limits that afternoon, engaging in street fights with ISIL militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1101_184-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1101-184">[184]</a></sup> Shortly after, the Iraqi Army announced that they had captured Mosul's state television building on the city's left bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> The Gogjali district was reported to be under Iraqi control by the evening, while Iraqi Army's 9th Division and the 3rd Brigade had entered the neighborhood of Judaydat al-Mufti on the left bank of Mosul. Near midnight, the Iraqi war media office reported that airstrikes had killed 116 militants inside Mosul including 29 in Ghabat, 10 at an ISIL headquarters, 10 at a weapons depot and 67 at a hotel pool. They also stated that Iraqi forces suffered no casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1101_184-2"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1101-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Iraqi forces captured 2 villages on the northern front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1101_184-3"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1101-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brigadier Saad Maan, the spokesperson of Iraq’s Interior Ministry, stated that the plan of the joint command in Nineveh was going faster than the Army had planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In the western front, at least fifteen <a href="/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces" title="Popular Mobilization Forces">PMU</a> fighters were killed when they entered abandoned villages booby-trapped with explosives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> ISIL also executed fifty deserters in Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kills50_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kills50-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>2 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 2 November, ISOF continued fighting remaining ISIL fighters in the eastern section of Gogjali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1102_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1102-191">[191]</a></sup> Iraqi Brigadier General Haider Fadhil said his troops were forced to hold their positions in eastern Mosul as poor weather conditions were limiting visibility for drones and aircraft, and preventing them from advancing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Meanwhile, eight militants were killed in Mosul by Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>The PMU announced that it had captured 115 km² that day after fierce fighting with ISIL, including six villages, and had surrounded three ISIL-held villages. They also claimed that they had reached a highway to the southwest of Mosul and had cut the first supply line to Mosul from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raqqa" title="Raqqa">Raqqa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1102_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1102-191">[191]</a></sup> The Iraqi Army in the southern front launched an offensive in the morning to recapture <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a> and engaged in heavy fighting with the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Iraqi Federal Police captured two villages in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1102_191-2"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1102-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>3 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>ISIL released an audio file purportedly from their leader <a href="/wiki/Abu_Bakr_al-Baghdadi" title="Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi">Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi</a>, in which he said he was "confident of victory" in Mosul, and urged ISIL fighters not to retreat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the Iraqi Army's 9th Armored Division was reported to have entered the neighborhood of al-Intisar in eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1103_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1103-196">[196]</a></sup> while Mosul's <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Bridge" title="Fifth Bridge">Fifth Bridge</a>, located over the Tigris river, was destroyed by airstrikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>U.S. and Iraqi authorities stated the offensive was "ahead of schedule" while Brigadier Saad Maan stated that the priority of protecting civilian lives and infrastructure would possibly slow their advance into the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>4 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Iraqi Army recaptured six districts in Mosul, including the eastern district of al-Zahra of which they claimed to have captured 90%. They were also forced to withdraw from Karama district because of heavy resistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Meanwhile, ISIL was reported to be abducting Mosul's boys to use as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_soldiers" title="Child soldiers">child soldiers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kills50_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kills50-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>5 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>Fighting continued in the morning, with clashes most intense in the neighborhood of al-Bakr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap1105_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap1105-200">[200]</a></sup> The eastern neighborhoods of Kirkukli and al-Zahra in the east and Al-Tahrir in the north-east were under Iraqi control while the southern neighborhoods of Qudes and Karama reportedly remained under ISIL control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1105_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1105-201">[201]</a></sup> Fighting resumed in the Gogjali district, after militants emerged via tunnels during the night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1105_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1105-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>CNN's <a href="/wiki/Arwa_Damon" title="Arwa Damon">Arwa Damon</a>, who was embedded with ISOF in Mosul, reported being trapped for 28 hours near the neighborhoods of Kirkukli and Khadraa after an ambush on their military convoy forced them to run into buildings for cover and hide among civilians. Despite multiple soldiers being injured, backup forces were unable to assist as they were also under attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>ISIL claimed it had killed fifteen Iraqi soldiers and destroyed six military vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1105_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1105-201">[201]</a></sup> Meanwhile, satellite images released by private U.S. firm <a href="/wiki/Stratfor" title="Stratfor">Stratfor</a> revealed ISIL had installed defenses including rubble blocking main routes to the city center, rows of concrete barricades, and earthen <a href="/wiki/Berm" title="Berm">berms</a>. The images also showed evidence that ISIL had leveled buildings and cleared the terrain around a former military base on the west bank and around the <a href="/wiki/Mosul_International_Airport" title="Mosul International Airport">Mosul International Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap1105_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap1105-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Iraqi army continued its assault on three fronts to <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1105_201-2"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1105-201">[201]</a></sup> In the early afternoon, Iraqi forces entered the town center with heavy clashes continuing. ISIL fighters were reportedly traveling by motorcycle to avoid airstrikes. During the night, Hamam al-Alil was reported to have been retaken by Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1105_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1105-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>6 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 6 November, Iraqi forces in southwestern front stated that they are 4 kilometres (2.5 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Mosul_International_Airport" title="Mosul International Airport">Mosul International Airport</a> after taking control of <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a> the previous day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> They also stormed the Al-Sada district, their first entrance into northern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The Iraq War Media Office announced that Abu Hamza al-Ansari, a key ISIL leader from Algeria, was killed in southern Mosul during clashes with the Iraqi Army's 15th Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ansari_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ansari-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Blogger <i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i> reported that ISIL had begun installing bombs around residential buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a Kurdish official stated that three militants had been killed in an uprising by civilians in eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ansari_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-ansari-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>7 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Peshmerga, backed by coalition airstrikes, launched an offensive from three fronts in the morning to take the town of <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a>, which was still held by ISIL and had been surrounded for about two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1107_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1107-207">[207]</a></sup> About 100 to 200 ISIL militants were estimated to be left in the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> In the early afternoon, the Iraqi troops also advanced on the town of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Keppe" title="Tel Keppe">Tel Keppe</a>, north of Mosul.own was reported to be fully under Peshmerga control, though ISIL pockets remained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1107_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1107-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the southern front, <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a>, which had been reported to be under Iraqi control two days earlier, was fully captured by pro-government forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In eastern Mosul, the ISOF surrounded the neighborhoods of Karama, Malayyin al-Salasa, Shquq Khazraa, Zahra, Karkuli, Aden, and Zahabi. The Iraqi Army's 9th armored division and the 3rd Brigade liberated the village of Manarat Shabak east of the city, and made an incursion into the eastern Mosul neighborhoods of Hay Intisar, Judaydah al-Mufti, and Hay Shaima.
