Meanwhile, the Iraqi Federal Police captured two villages near Hammam Al-Alil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1107_207-2"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1107-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>8 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Peshmerga killed twelve ISIL fighters trying to flee <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> In the western front, PMU forces were reported to have advanced to a distance of 25 km towards strategically important <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a> military air base, south of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> CJTF–OIR also stated it had carried out an airstrike on an ISIL headquarters building near Tal Afar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> ISIL senior commander Mahmoud Shukri al-Nuaimi was also reported to have been killed in a coalition airstrike in western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1111_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1111-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>9 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>ISOF captured majority of the Intisar district in southern Mosul while ISIL had reportedly deployed armed child soldiers in Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Aid agencies were unable to reach Mosul's neighborhoods retaken by Iraqi forces because of the danger of boobytraps and snipers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>10 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>In eastern Mosul, the Golden Division (controlling Zahra district and at least half of Aden district where clashes were ongoing) as well as elements of the 9th division (controlling Intisar district) were reported to be regrouping and clearing neighborhoods once occupied by ISIL, as well as screening residents fleeing from Mosul for any militants hiding among them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> On the southern front, pro-government forces advanced towards the ancient city of <a href="/wiki/Nimrud" title="Nimrud">Nimrud</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Iraqi officials announced that the new ISIL war official, Khaled al-Mitwiti, had been killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> while the Abbas Rajab village was captured by Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>11 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On the southern front, Iraqi forces were preparing to advance up the western bank of the Tigris River toward <a href="/wiki/Mosul_International_Airport" title="Mosul International Airport">Mosul International Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> In eastern Mosul, Iraqi forces launched a new offensive to regain control of the neighborhood of Karkukli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> Iraqi anti-terror units were reported to have entered the Qadesiyya neighborhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>12 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 12 November, heavy clashes were reported in the al-Salam neighborhood of east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rudaw_Media_Network_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rudaw_Media_Network-222">[222]</a></sup> Iraqi Army announced that it had captured al-Arbajiya district and was clearing the adjacent al-Qadisiya al-Thaniya district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> They also reached Palestine neighborhood in southeast Mosul and were engaged in battle with ISIL in the Quds neighborhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rudaw_Media_Network_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rudaw_Media_Network-222">[222]</a></sup> The PMU announced that the <a href="/wiki/Sinjar_Resistance_Units" title="Sinjar Resistance Units">Sinjar Resistance Units</a> (YBŞ) as its part, had started the operation to capture villages around <a href="/wiki/Sinjar" title="Sinjar">Sinjar</a> from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a number of its senior leaders were killed by a coalition air strike in east Mosul, ISIL imposed a curfew in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> A local source also stated that the group was evacuating families of its fighters from west to east Mosul, denoting a severe collapse of defenses on the western front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Its fighters were meanwhile using drones for surveillance as well as suicide bombers and snipers against the Iraqi Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rudaw_Media_Network_222-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rudaw_Media_Network-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>13 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 13 November, Iraqi forces recaptured the ancient Assyrian city of <a href="/wiki/Nimrud" title="Nimrud">Nimrud</a> as well as the adjacent modern town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Iraqi forces meanwhile captured the Karkojli neighborhood in eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Brig. Gen. Maan al Saadi, the commander of the 2nd Group of ISOF, stated ISIL was collapsing and losing control, with Iraqi forces now only two days away from seizing a neighborhood where they planned to fight for four days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>14 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 14 November, thirty ISIL fighters, including senior leaders, were killed as PMU forces captured the village of al-Abbas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3km_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-3km-231">[231]</a></sup> They also captured two more villages, and stated ISIL received severe human and material losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Meanwhile, twenty militants were killed in airstrikes by the Iraqi air Force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pro-government forces on the southern front captured the village of Bo Youssef and were 3 kilometres (1.9 mi) from Mosul airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3km_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-3km-231">[231]</a></sup> ISIL meanwhile launched three attacks using rockets filled with mustard gas on Qayyarah, causing seven casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>15 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 15 November, 49 militants were killed in airstrikes by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> on the al-Bakr neighborhood of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Troops of the Golden Division meanwhile began storming areas in northern and eastern Mosul, including the neighborhoods of al-Akhaa, al-Bakr and al-Hadbaa. Two car bombs were destroyed while three suicide bombers were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> On the Western front, the Badr Organization announced that it had captured two villages and advanced 10 kilometers in the western axis of the offensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>16 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 16 November, fourteen civilians were killed by ISIL in the al-Zahraa neighborhood under government control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> Airstrikes by the US-led coalition meanwhile destroyed 4 watercrafts, 6 mortar systems, 2 fighting positions, 2 vehicles, a bunker and a building held by ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>PMF also took control of <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a> military airbase west of the city Mosul, killing a large number of ISIL fighters in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>18 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 18 November, in the West, PMF were securing and clearing <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a> military airbase, which they had captured from ISIL two days earlier, and preparing the assault on the city proper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> In the vicinity, they were attacking further villages, in an area infamous for Sunni Islamist militancy and outstanding support for ISIL among the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> PMF control had already been established in over 16 villages in the surrounding area, during preceding days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>20 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Anti-Terrorism Directorate said in a statement aired by the state-owned television that the Anti-Terrorism forces managed to liberate the areas of Hayy Adan, al-Akhaa and the water project in Mosul, within the eastern axis of Nineveh liberation operations. The Wali of Islamic State in Hayy Adan, Marwan Hamed Saleh al-Hayali, was killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016_Mosul_Offensive_(Mosul_Surrounds).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1491" data-file-width="2560" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg/300px-2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg/450px-2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg/600px-2016_Mosul_Offensive_%28Mosul_Surrounds%29.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016_Mosul_Offensive_(Mosul_Surrounds).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Infographic of Mosul control lines (around 22 November 2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>22 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 22 November, in Mosul ISIL fighters were reported targeting Iraqi special forces with rockets and mortars as they slowly advanced in the densely populated Zohour neighborhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> Four of the five Tigris bridges were hit by coalition airstrikes within the past 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baaj_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-baaj-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>Far to the West at the Syrian border, near the town of Baaj, four Islamic State commanders were captured in a U.S. special operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baaj_247-1"><a href="#cite_note-baaj-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>23 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 23 November, to the West, PMF reported cutting the road between <a href="/wiki/Sinjar" title="Sinjar">Sinjar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a>, their Shia component groups advancing from the South linking up with the <a href="/wiki/Sinjar_Resistance_Units" title="Sinjar Resistance Units">Sinjar Resistance Units</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Az%C3%AEdxan_Women%27s_Units" title="Êzîdxan Women's Units">Êzîdxan Women's Units</a> to the North, thus completing the encirclement of the Mosul pocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>25 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>50 ISIL fighters were killed and 32 others were arrested with Iraqi Federal Police continuing the operation to clear the area south of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>30 November</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 30 November, PMF said they captured 12 villages from ISIL in the <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a> area over the past five days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of November, the Iraqi military assessed that it had taken control of 19 neighbourhoods in eastern Mosul during the month, constituting somewhat less than 30 percent of the area of Mosul east of the <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">Tigris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> While the "Golden Division" Special Operations Forces persistently advanced into East Mosul, the 9th Division took one neighbourhood in the southeast, the 16th Division had not yet breached Mosul city limits from the north, and the 15th Division, advancing from the southwest, was still several kilometres away from western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="December:_Advancing_towards_the_Syrian_border">December: Advancing towards the Syrian border</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: December: Advancing towards the Syrian border">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl>
<dt>4 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>2 ISIL leaders, Abu Turq and Falah al-Rashidi, were killed in airstrikes by the anti-ISIL coalition on 4 December. Al-Rishdi was involved in the group's use of VBIEDs and was killed in Mosul. Abu Turq was killed in Shirqat and was a financial facilitator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>6 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>20 airstrikes by the US-led coalition were heard on the morning of 6 December following an assault on the city's strategic main bridge that was held by ISIL. In the overnight hours, ISIL launched a counter-attack in the southeastern area of Mosul, near al-Salam; however, casualty figures from either side were not announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_Times_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times-254">[254]</a></sup> PMU meanwhile stated that it had captured the southern section of Tal Abta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="960" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png/350px-Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png/525px-Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png/700px-Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_as_of_7-Dec-2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ongoing battle as of December 7th, 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>7 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Following the overnight ISIL attack, Iraqi forces continued to secure the al-Salam area, capturing al-Salam hospital. However, ISIL recaptured the hospital after a counterattack which destroyed or disabled 20 Iraqi vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>9 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi Joint Operations Command announced on 9 December that they had captured the three districts of Saha, Adel and Tahrir. It further added that Iraqi forces had captured 27 districts of Mosul with clashes ongoing in 4 districts. Lieutenant-General Abdul Ameer Yarallah meanwhile stated that three factories making car bombs in Mosul and three weapons warehouses were destroyed by Iraqi airstrikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>11 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The CTS forces mentioned that they had captured another district of east Mosul, al-Nour neighborhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>12 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Iraqi federal police said that three of their brigades, initially meant to advance from the southwest toward the airport, were redeployed to join the three "Golden Division" counterterrorism brigades in the east of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STRATFOR_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-STRATFOR-259">[259]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>13 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>CTS commander Abdul Wahab al-Saedi stated that there were only 6 districts left to be captured by the CTS forces in East Mosul and they had already captured 32 of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> While the PMF to the West continued clearing villages in the desert region of the ISIL heartland, on 13 December it was reported that the Badr militia was targeting villages around Tal Afar to "surround Daesh and tighten the noose around them", and Kata'ib Hezbollah advanced further west towards the Syrian border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> Abu Dur al-Tunsi and Bilal al-Shawash, two Tunisian ISIL military commanders, reportedly deserted after they were attacked by Iraqi members. According to the head of Nineveh Media Centre's Raafat al-Zarari, the local militants were being made to fight at the front lines, while some non-Iraqi commanders didn't engage in direct clashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tunisiancommanders_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tunisiancommanders-29">[29]</a></sup> CTS forces meanwhile captured al-Falah Oula and al-Falah Thaniya districts later in the day while PMU captured 7 villages near Tal Afar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>14 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 14 December, 70 ISIL fighters including 20 senior leaders as well as their bodyguards were killed in Iraqi airstrikes on Tel Abta where they were holding a meeting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> Meanwhile, 40 civilians were killed in airstrikes and shelling in east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> A number of militants who attempted to launch suicide attacks in 3 districts of east Mosul were also killed, with some of their booby-trapped vehicles also destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>15 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Iraqi Federal Police announced on 15 December the capture of Saleh Najem Abdullah, the Media Center Official of ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> CTS commander Abdul Ghani al-Assadi meanwhile announced that the first phase of retaking the eastern shores of the city was completed, with CTS forces capturing 40 out of 56 districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>16 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>PMF were in the process to take control of further villages to the south and southwest of <a href="/wiki/Tal_Afar" title="Tal Afar">Tal Afar</a>, after capturing Tel Abth district, home to almost 50,000 people and a major strategic ISIL stronghold, in the past days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STRATFOR_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-STRATFOR-259">[259]</a></sup> Iraqi forces meanwhile repelled 4 ISIL attacks, killing 174 militants and destroying 13 SVBIEDs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>17 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>An airstrike by the US-led coalition near Mosul destroyed 5 buildings used by ISIL in addition to quantities of weapons and equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>18 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Brig. Gen. Taher al-Sammak of Iraq's SWAT forces stated that the 9th Division, with the assistance of CTS, had started attacking al-Wehda district of east Mosul in order to regain control of al-Salam hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>19 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Captain Iyad Ziad of Nineveh Operations Command stated that Iraqi forces had stormed into al-Mazare’ area after retaking large parts of al-Wahda in southeastern Mosul and also killed 14 ISIL fighters including 4 suicide bombers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> 4 PMF fighters were meanwhile killed in an ISIL attack on Abu Senam village near Tel Afar. The group also shelled Tel Afar Airport and destroyed 2 PMF vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>21 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>U.S. Air Force Brigadier General Matthew Isler announced on 21 December that pro-government forces had entered a planned operational refit which included repairing vehicles, re-supplying ammunition and preparing for the next stage of the battle. He also stated that they had captured more than a quarter of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>22 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The UN stated, on 22 December, that 4 Iraqi aid workers and 7 civilians were killed by mortar fire. Later, ISIL launched a triple suicide bomb attack at a market in Gogjali. 23 people, including 15 civilians, were killed in the attacks, according to the Iraqi military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> The Iraqi Ministry of Defense says the Iraqi Air Force bombarded a gathering of Islamic State members, south of Tal Abta area, killing 20 leaders and 50 members, based on intelligence information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>23 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Iraqi Army captured the Mosul Police Academy headquarters in Al-Qahira district on 23 December. This was their first major advance since suspension of military operations a week earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>24 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>U.S. Army Colonel Brett G. Sylvia stated on 24 December that American soldiers assisting Iraqi forces will be embedded more extensively and will partner with additional formations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> Iraqi Prime Minister Haider al-Abadi stated that Iraqi forces are in control of over a third of Mosul. Iraqi Joint Operations Command spokesperson Yahia Rasoul stated that Iraqi forces control 44% of Nineveh Governate. He added that CTS forces control 40 districts in east Mosul, while the Iraqi Army's 9th Battalion held six districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> Meanwhile 10 civilians were killed due to ISIL shelling in eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>25 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>At least 97 militants were killed in Mosul during the day according to Operations Commander Lieutenant-General Abdulamir Rashid Yarallah. He stated that an attack by ISIL on police stations south of Abuyosif area resulted in the death of 21 IS fighters. He also added that another attack at Al-Intisar, Salam and Al-Shaima'a neighborhoods had killed 51 jihadists, while the anti-ISIL coalition killed 25 militants in airstrikes on their hideout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> CTS reportedly stormed into the Al-Quds district later in the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>26 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Commander of Nineveh Operations Major General Najim al-Jabouri announced on 26 December that new military reinforcements had arrived in the Mosul neighborhoods retaken by Iraqi forces, both to enhance their presence and to prepare themselves to storm into the remaining areas of the eastern side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> Lieutenant Colonel Stuart James, commander of an American battalion assisting the Iraqi forces, meanwhile stated that a new advance in Mosul would begin within days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> The Iraqi Defence Ministry meanwhile stated that 10 militants were killed and 14 ISIL cannons were destroyed in coalition airstrikes in east of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> According to a military official, another 5 ISIL fighters were captured for information after some troops of the 16th Division, disguised as ISIL members, infiltrated inside the Owaiza area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>27 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>The ISIL-run Amaq News Agency stated that the anti-ISIL coalition had destroyed the Old Bridge, the last functioning bridge in Mosul. The US-led Coalition, meanwhile, stated that it had disabled a Mosul bridge with airstrikes without providing the details.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>29 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces launched the second phase of the battle on 29 December, pushing from three directions into eastern Mosul districts. Iraqi soldiers and Federal Police entered about half a dozen southeastern districts. CTS meanwhile advanced in al-Quds and Karama districts. In the third front, Iraqi soldiers also pushed toward the northern limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> Jabouri stated that they were ordered by the Prime Minister to reach the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigris_River" title="Tigris River">Tigris River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> An ISIL headquarters in al-Thobat district was reportedly destroyed in coalition airstrikes, killing 12 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> Later in the day, the commander of the operation declared that they had captured 2 villages to the north of Mosul, killing 70 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> Iraqi forces had captured half of al-Quds by early afternoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> The Iraqi military later announced that they had killed more than 200 militants during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>30 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi security forces advanced in several areas on 30 December. In the northern front, the 16th Division stormed the Habdaa district while also trying to cut off the supply lines to Tel Kayf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> Meanwhile, ISIL was reported to have evacuated family members of its foreign fighters from four districts in western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> 2 ISIL attacks in eastern Mosul were later repelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> Ammar al-Haweidi, who is an elite leader of ISIL was reported to have been killed by the Iraqi Federal Police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> Clashes broke out again in one of the villages reported to be captured a day earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>31 December</dt>
</dl>
<p>Heavy clashes occurred on the southeastern and northern fronts of Mosul on 31 December. An Iraqi Army officer deployed in the southeastern front reported that their advances were slowed down due to heavy clashes and difficulty in differentiating between civilians and militants. Iraqi forces on the northern front advances towards the periphery of Mosul, with an officer stating that heavy clashes were ongoing in the Argoob area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> The CTS destroyed four VBIEDs when ISIL tried to attack them in the street linking al-Ta’mim neighborhood and the garage area in east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">U.S. military</a> meanwhile stated that its airstrikes on a van carrying ISIL fighters at a hospital compound parking lot might have killed civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="January_2017:_Second_phase_and_reaching_the_Tigris">January 2017: Second phase and reaching the Tigris</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: January 2017: Second phase and reaching the Tigris">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl>
<dt>1 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces continued their advance on 1 January 2017. The military announced that it had captured a part of the Karama district, and a federal police officer stated that they had taken near complete control of Intissar and Siha districts, and were clearing the Salam district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> CTS linked up with Rapid Response Division during the day at the edge of al-Intissar and al-Quds. Staff Lieutenant General Abdulwahab al-Saadi, a top CTS commander, stated that Iraqi forces had captured more than 60% of east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> Iraqi Defence Ministry's War Media Cell announced during the day that Iraqi forces had captured Yunus al-Sabaawi and Yafa districts in the southeastern part of the city. Lt. Col. Eyad al-Awsyi said that they had also completely captured al-Intissar, and were nearing completion of capturing Karama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> Federal Police announced later in the day that they had captured the Gogjali-Intsar road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> They also stated during the day that they had captured the strategic No.60 Street to the southeast of Mosul. Army major Ali Mohsen meanwhile said that the Iraqi Army had captured al-Malayeen, al-Kindi and al-Arabi al-Thania districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>2 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>CTS announced on 2 January that they had completely captured al-Karama district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> Sabah al-Numan, the CTS spokesman, later stated that they were clearing the remaining militants in North Karama. ISIL meanwhile cut off a strategic road linking Mosul and Baghdad. The group also shelled Shirqat, after attacking a military barracks near Baiji and seizing weapons. According to the Mayor of Shirqat, they had seized 3 checkpoints on the main road between the city and Baiji. Iraqi authorities later said that they had regained control of the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>3 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces stormed three districts on 3 January and killed 50 militants during clashes in 2 of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> The operation commander said that Iraqi Air Force airstrikes had destroyed the office of ISIL's <a href="/wiki/Hisbah" title="Hisbah">hisbah</a> police located on Mosul-Tel Afar road, and several warfare utilities of the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> The Federal Police said that it had destroyed the headquarters of Jund al-Khilafa (Soldiers of Caliphate), an ISIL explosives factory and a drone headquarters in al-Mithaq district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> The Iraqi Army announced later that CTS had captured Karama industrial neighborhood, the Industrial district, the Karama Silo (a flour mill), and a Mercedes Company building during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> The Ministry of Defense later announced that Iraqi forces had captured the area of exhibitions and the commercial complex to the south of Ta'mim district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> The forces later announced that they had captured Al-Hay al-Senai and al-Mithaq districts as well as the Maaridh area to the east of Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>4 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces cleared Mithaq district and advanced in al-Wahda on 4 January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> said that civilian casualties had started increasing as they advanced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> The Joint Operations Command said that the Federal Police and 9th Division had captured Wahda after heavy clashes, bringing them closer to the city center, and that ISIL counter-attacks in southeastern Mosul had been repelled, with the death of about 40 militants and destruction of 7 VBIEDs. Iraqi forces also advanced in al-Salam, Palestine, al-Shaimaa, Domiez and Sumer districts amid heavy clashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> The Federal Police meanwhile announced the killing of Abu Marawan al-Hadithi, an ISIL leader. Lt.-Gen. Ra'ed Shaker also said that Iraqi forces had cleared al-Wahda, al-Moallemin and Sumer districts, and had captured the Mosul-Kirkuk road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> and the anti-ISIL coalition stated that American advisers had entered Mosul along with Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>5 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Lt.-Gen. Talib Shaghati stated on 5 January that Iraqi forces had captured about 65-70% of east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> During the day, the Federal Police said that they had destroyed three ISIL drones in east Mosul. An attack on PMU near Tal Afar was meanwhile reportedly repelled, with the deaths of 35 militants including senior recruitment agent Abu Qaswara al-Shami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> The Federal Police announced that 1,700 ISIL fighters had been killed in the second phase. General Raed Shaker Jawdat stated that the group's headquarters in Nineveh province had been destroyed and Iraqi forces had captured eight districts in the second phase, thus bringing the entire southeastern section of Mosul under their control. He added that they had also captured drone factories, five car bomb manufacturing plants, an electrical plant, a windmill and several schools. He said that all the remaining districts in east Mosul had been surrounded and would be stormed soon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>6 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 6 January, CTS was reported to have stormed the al-Muthanna district during an overnight raid across the al-Khawsar river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> A CTS spokesman later said that ISIL had been driven out of the district and dozens of militants killed in airstrikes by the anti-ISIL coalition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> This was the first time that Iraqi forces had entered Mosul from the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> They also launched an assault on the Hadbaa apartment complex in the northern front, and faced heavy clashes later in the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>7 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces continued their advance on 7 January, coming within several hundred metres of the Tigris river. During the day CTS said that they had captured the al-Gharfan district (previously known as al-Baath) and had entered Wahda district. The military later announced that they had captured a hospital complex in Wahda. Meanwhile, a spokesman of the anti-ISIL coalition stated that ISIL had deliberately damaged the fourth bridge as Iraqi forces advanced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> Staff Lieutenant General Yarallah said that Iraqi forces had captured Al-Salam Hospital, Al-Shifa Hospital and the Faculty of Medicine, a medical college. They had also captured ISIL's command center and two prisons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> He later said that CTS had captured Rifaq, Atibaa 1st and Atibaa 2nd districts, and well as the Hadbaa residential complex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>8 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 8 January, al-Saadi said that CTS troops advancing towards Sukkar and Baladiyat districts had been attacked by ISIL from a historic hill, but had been repelled with the help of coalition warplanes, killing dozens of militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> Security sources said that Iraqi forces were shelling ISIL's positions in al-Kindi district in preparation for storming it later, while the 9th division and Federal Police had launched an attack on Sumer and Domiz districts in the southeastern front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> The CTS spokesman said that Iraqi forces had reached the Tigris river for the first time in the offensive, advancing towards the eastern side of the fourth bridge. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brett_McGurk" title="Brett McGurk">Brett McGurk</a>, USA's envoy to the anti-ISIL coalition, said that ISIL's defences in eastern Mosul were showing signs of collapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> An ISIL attack on Hadbaa apartments was later reportedly repelled, with the death of about 10 militants and destruction of 4 VBIEDs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> PMU meanwhile stated that they had repelled an ISIL attack near Adaya, located to the west of Mosul, killing about 10 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>9 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi military stated on 9 January that CTS had captured the Baladiyat district in the eastern front while the Federal Police and Iraqi Army had captured Domiz and Palestine districts in the southeastern front. CTS also carried out operations to clear Furqan and Atiba districts. An ISIL attack in Furqaan was repelled according to the military, resulting in deaths of 30 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> Iraqi Defense Ministry’s War Media Cell meanwhile stated that Iraqi Air Force killed 25 militants in airstrikes in eastern Mosul while airstrikes by the anti-ISIL coalition killed about 20 militants in al-Abra village near Tal Afar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup> The group which was still in control of the city's water stations, was reported to have cut the water supply to more than 30 districts captured by Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> ISOF meanwhile surrounded the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mosul" title="University of Mosul">University of Mosul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>10 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi Joint Operations Command stated on 10 January that CTS forces had captured the Sukkar and al-Dhubbat districts while advancing in Siddeeq and al-Maliyah districts. Several governmental offices including the communication complex, provincial electricity department and a security headquarters were also captured according to it. It also stated that ISIL had blown up two bridges in order to prevent Iraqi forces from attacking western Mosul. It added that in the southeastern front, the Federal police and Iraqi Army pushed further into al-Salam, Palestine, Sumer, Yarimja and Sahiron districts. Regarding the northern front it stated that Iraqi Army advanced further into al-Hadbaa while capturing northern part of Sabaa Nisaan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a security source stated that Iraqi Air Force had conducted airstrikes on headquarters of ISIL's Australian leaders in Mosul, killing the commander of Australian Brigade Khaled Sharouf, also known as Abu Mosab al-Australi along with three of his aides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>11 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces continued advancing on 11 January with military officials stating that the CTS had advanced in the Sadeeq district and were firing into the adjacent Hadbaa. Iraqi forces also clashed with ISIL in the southern front during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>12 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>CTS spokesman al-Numan stated on 12 January that CTS had captured 7th Nissan and Sadeeq districts, successfully linking up with Iraqi Army advancing in Hadbaa district. He claimed that Iraqi forces were now in control of about 85% of eastern Mosul. The Rapid Response Division meanwhile advanced in Sumer and Sahiroun districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> Iraqi Defense Ministry’s War Media Cell stated that a senior ISIL leader was killed along with his companions in an airstrike by Iraqi Air Force on their camp in al-Amel district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> Security sources stated that 90 militants were killed in airstrikes by Iraqi Air Force on Yaramja district while local sources stated that 3 militants including a senior member in charge of ISIL's prisons were killed in a drone strike in western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> The operation command later announced that Iraqi Army had captured Sumer and Sahiroun districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> PMU meanwhile stated it had captured 3 villages near Tel Abta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> The operation command later also announced that Iraqi forces had captured al-Salam district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>13 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>The operation command announced on 13 January that CTS had reached the second bridge of the city, which is also called the "Freedom Bridge". Yarallah stated that in response, ISIL had destroyed all five bridges of the city, in order to slow the Iraqi advance towards western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup> CTS later announced they had reached the Old Bridge also known as the "Iron Bridge" and stormed the University of Mosul, capturing a part of its complex later in the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> The operation command later announced that CTS had captured al-Kafa'at district in eastern front as well as al-Sadriya, al-Naser and al-Faisaliyah in central part of East Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> Iraqi Army also captured the Hadbaa district during the day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup> while Yarallah declared that CTS had captured a government complex which included the Nineveh Governorate and council buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>14 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Spokesman Abdel Amir al-Mohammedawi stated on 14 January that the Rapid Response Division had captured the Yarimja area as well as a field hospital ISIL was using. A military statement meanwhile announced that the Federal Police had captured the highway between Mosul and <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">Kirkuk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup> Iraqi forces later completely captured the University of Mosul, in addition to the eastern side of a third bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup> Meanwhile, 10 militants were reportedly killed or wounded in infighting between a group of ISIL fighters who fled towards west Mosul and the leaders in western side due to mutual accusations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-357"><a href="#cite_note-357">[357]</a></sup> An airstrike by CJTF-OIR on the house of a senior ISIL leader was reported to have resulted in deaths of around 30 civilians. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CENTCOM" title="CENTCOM">CENTCOM</a> stated that the allegation will be investigated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-358"><a href="#cite_note-358">[358]</a></sup> Suicide bombings were carried out by an Iraqi, Tajik, and an Uzbek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>15 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 15 January, Iraqi forces carried out a sweeping operation in the University of Mosul for any hiding militants while continuing their advancement along the Tigris river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup> The operation command later announced that the Iraqi Army had captured al-Kafaat Thani (Second) district in the northern front while CTS had captured Andalus in the eastern front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-361"><a href="#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-362"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>16 January</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png/220px-Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png/330px-Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png/440px-Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ruins_of_the_Mosque_of_Yunus.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The ruins of the Nabi Yunus mosque after it was captured by Iraqi forces</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Clashes occurred in Shurta and Andalus districts on 16 January. By this point, Iraqi forces had taken complete control of the river banks in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-363"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> The operation command during the day announced that the Army had captured Kindi and Qairawan districts while CTS had captured Jammasa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> CTS spokesman al-Numan later announced that they had captured the Nabi Yunus area including the <a href="/wiki/Mosques_and_shrines_of_Mosul#The_Mosque_of_the_Prophet_Yunus_.28Jonah.29" title="Mosques and shrines of Mosul">Nabi Yunus shrine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_(17-01-17).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="960" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png/350px-Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png/525px-Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png/700px-Battle_of_Mosul_%2817-01-17%29.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Mosul_(17-01-17).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ongoing battle as of January 17th, 2017.</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>17 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>al-Numan stated that CTS was now in complete control of Shurta and Andalus. He also stated that they had pushed into Eastern Nineveh and Souq al-Ghanam districts. A separate military statement announced that CTS had also captured al-Muhandiseen district. Meanwhile the Iraqi Army in the northern front stormed the Kindi military base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-366"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> Yarallah later announced that CTS had captured Nineveh al-Sharqiya, Bab-Shams and Souq al-Ghanam districts in the eastern front. He added that they had also captured Nu'maniya and Uttshana districts in addition to storming the adjacent al-Jazair district. Regarding the northern front, he stated that Iraqi Army had captured the Kindi military base, the former headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Division_(Iraq)" title="2nd Division (Iraq)">2nd Division</a> as well as the nearby al-Kindi facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-367"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-368"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> Iraqi forces also succeeded in capturing all five bridges of the city during the day while al-Saadi announced they had also captured the Zaraei district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-369"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> CTS also captured Al Jazair, Al Derkazlih, Al Seuis and Sanharib districts during the day. Yarallah also stated that they had captured the Grand Mosque of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-370"><a href="#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> Colonel John Dorrian stated during the day that Iraqi forces were in control of 85-90% of east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup> Iraqi Prime Minister al-Abadi meanwhile stated that Iraqi forces had begun moving against ISIL in western Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>18 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Lieutenant-General Talib Shaghati announced on 18 January that CTS had captured all the districts of east Mosul they were tasked with taking, and that Iraqi forces were almost in complete control of the eastern side. A military statement announced that a few parts of the city in north had yet to be captured by the Iraqi Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-374"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> Shaghati also stated that all five bridges of the city were under control of Iraqi forces. During the day, CTS captured the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">Nineveh</a> ruins as well as the adjacent Tal Nirgal area. The operation command meanwhile announced that Iraqi Army had captured al-Qadhiyah district and were fighting on the edges of al-Arabi district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-376"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> PMU meanwhile announced that they had captured 2 areas in the Nineveh Plains region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>19 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>On 19 January, the military statements announced that the Iraqi Army had captured the town of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Keppe" title="Tel Keppe">Tel Kayf</a> (after a nearly 3-month-long siege),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tel_Keppe_recaptured_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Keppe_recaptured-378">[378]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tel_Kaif_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Kaif-379">[379]</a></sup> as well as the Nineveh Oberoi hotel and the "Palaces" area on the eastern bank of the Tigris. Clashes were still ongoing in the Al-Arabi District. Meanwhile, McGurk announced that over 50 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watercrafts" title="Watercrafts">watercrafts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barges" title="Barges">barges</a> being used by ISIL to supply its members in eastern Mosul were destroyed in airstrikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup> Iraqi Air Force carried out an airstrike in al-Zerai area in Mosul, reportedly killing five ISIL leaders including Abdel Wahed Khodier, assistant to <a href="/wiki/Abu_Bakr_al-Baghdadi" title="Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi">Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi</a>; the Islamic Police Chief in Nineveh, Ahmed Khodier Sayer al-Juwan and Agriculture Minister in Tal Afar and Mahlabiya, Abdel Karim Khodier Sayer al-Juwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup> Yarallah meanwhile announced that Iraqi forces had also captured the Fadiliyah district and Jaber ibn Hayyan military facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup> Iraqi forces also captured the Ghabat area during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-major-district_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-major-district-383">[383]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>20 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Yarallah announced on 20 January that the 9th Division had captured the <a href="/wiki/Free_economic_zone" title="Free economic zone">free zone</a> in the northern sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-384"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup> Iraqi forces also captured a pharmaceutical plant to the north of Mosul as well as Al-Arabi 1 district. They also clashed with ISIL in Rashidiyah district. Meanwhile, CTS started clearing the districts they had captured in Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-385"><a href="#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-major-district_383-1"><a href="#cite_note-major-district-383">[383]</a></sup> Iraqi Air Forces also said that they carried out an airstrike targeting the regions of Tel Kaif and al-Sehaji, in northeastern Mosul, killing 88 militants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-386"><a href="#cite_note-386">[386]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>21 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi forces continued advancing in the outskirts of the city on 21 January. During the day, the operation command announced that the Iraqi Army had completely captured al-Arabi district as well as al-Qousiyat village, leaving some 40 militants killed and four car bombs destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-387"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> The CJTF-OIR also announced that between 19 and 21 January, they had targeted a flotilla of 90 boats and three barges being used by ISIL to cross the Tigris and escape the clashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-388"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup> On the same day, Coalition officials stated that the fight for west Mosul is expected to be tougher than the fight for east Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tougher_fight_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-tougher_fight-389">[389]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>22 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Iraqi military announced on 22 January that Iraqi forces had captured Al-Milayeen district and Al-Binaa al-Jahiz area as well as the Mosul-<a href="/wiki/Dohuk" title="Dohuk">Dohuk</a> road. By this point, only the Rashidiyah district was left under ISIL control in eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-390"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>23 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Iraqi defense ministry issued a statement earlier on 23 January on its website, announcing the complete capture of eastern Mosul. However it was later removed with fighting ongoing in Rashidiyah which the Iraqi Army entered during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-391"><a href="#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>24 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>The operation command announced on 24 January that Iraqi troops captured the Rashidiyah district as well as the villages of Ba'wiza, Shrikhan and Baysan. Iraqi Prime Minister al-Abadi later announced the "full liberation" of eastern Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-392"><a href="#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>25 January</dt>
</dl>
<p>Col. Khaled al-Jewari, from the Joint Operations Command, told DPA that ISIL executed a <i><a href="/wiki/Qadi" title="Qadi">qadi</a></i> (senior judge), along with other combat commanders, for escaping from the battle for eastern Mosul. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-393"><a href="#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile the PMU announced that they took over Tel Shana, a strategic hill in Salahuddin, after killing dozens of IS militants. It added that PMUs also took over the villages of ِArab Leith, Mohamed al-Awad and Ard Mosaltan after intense fights with the extremist group. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-394"><a href="#cite_note-394">[394]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_issues">Humanitarian issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Humanitarian issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Up to 1.5 million civilians live in the city, sparking concerns among various organizations of a large humanitarian crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp1017_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-afp1017-395">[395]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lise_Grande" title="Lise Grande">Lise Grande</a>, the United Nations' humanitarian coordinator in Iraq, stated, "In a worst-case scenario, we're literally looking at the single largest humanitarian operation in the world in 2016."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp1017_395-1"><a href="#cite_note-afp1017-395">[395]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> warned that massive civilian bloodshed was likely unless safe routes were allowed to let civilians flee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-396"><a href="#cite_note-396">[396]</a></sup> The U.S. government has accused ISIL of using Mosul civilians as <a href="/wiki/Human_shield" title="Human shield">human shields</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ISIL_abuses_and_abductions">ISIL abuses and abductions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: ISIL abuses and abductions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fears that civilians could be used as human shields by ISIL were realized as it was confirmed the group had been abducting civilians from villages for this purpose, which received widespread condemnation from human rights groups and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap1102_397-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap1102-397">[397]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-398"><a href="#cite_note-398">[398]</a></sup></p>
<p>ISIL has reportedly threatened to execute civilians trying to flee. Snipers, landmines and trenches are preventing people from attempting to escape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt1017_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-dt1017-54">[54]</a></sup> Iraqi officials, via radio broadcasts and leaflets dropped over the city, warned civilians to stay in their homes. Leaflets advised residents of various precautions to take including instructions to tape over their windows to protect from flying glass and to disconnect gas pipes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt1017_60-3"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1017-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399">[399]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after the battle began, news surfaced of ISIL kidnapping and executing civilians in Mosul. Pentagon spokesman Capt. Jeff Davis stated that ISIL was using civilians as human shields and holding people against their will in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1019_400-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1019-400">[400]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">International Business Times</a></i> reported that ISIL has forced boys from Mosul as young as 12 to fight for it, and that ISIL had trained the children to "behead prisoners and make suicide bombs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-401"><a href="#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup></p>
<p>An Iraqi intelligence source stated on 21 October that ISIL executed 284 men and boys abducted from Mosul for the purpose of using them as human shields. The civilians were shot and put in a mass grave. A United Nations official said the UN is "gravely worried" about the fate of 200 families from Samalia and 350 families from Najafia who were abducted Monday by ISIL, who could be used as human shields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1021_402-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1021-402">[402]</a></sup></p>
<p>UN sources stated that four people died from inhaling toxic fumes after ISIL set fire to the <a href="/wiki/Al-Mishraq" title="Al-Mishraq">Al-Mishraq</a> Chemical Factory on 23 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap1111_403-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap1111-403">[403]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 October, CNN reported that ISIL has been carrying out "retribution killings" of civilians as revenge for others welcoming Iraqi and Peshmerga troops in liberated villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1026_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1026-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Ravina Shamdasani, of the Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights, ISIL executed 232 people near Mosul in late October for defying its orders and had taken tens of thousands of people to use as human shields against advancing Iraqi forces. She claimed that ISIL "executed 42 civilians in <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a>, south of Mosul. Also on Wednesday ISIL executed 190 former Iraqi Security Forces for refusing to join them, in the Al Ghazlani base near Mosul."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Iraqi forces evacuated more than 1,000 civilians from the front lines surrounding Mosul on 26 October, moving them to the Khazir region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-404"><a href="#cite_note-404">[404]</a></sup> Civilians on the southern front had reported that their relatives had been taken by retreating ISIL fighters to be used as human shields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1026_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1026-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2016, Iraqi government has launched a military operation in Mosul to eject ISIL. Based on reports provided by the Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor, more than a million residents in Mosul are at risk and many of them were killed or used as human shields against the advance of Iraqi army. Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor warns that Iraqi government and international forces have to put an end to the humanitarian crisis in Mosul and provide its residents with their basic needs. ISIL has driven some of Mosul’s residents out of their neighborhoods while others were prevented from fleeing to the regions controlled by Iraqi army. Human rights are violated by both ISIL, which drove about 550 families from the villages of As-Semalyya and An-Nejafyya, and Iraqi troops which captured 1,500 civilians from mosques and schools in the Dybka refugee camp. On 21 October 2016, Another human rights violation committed by Iraqi army and police as they arrested almost hundreds of civilians and executing some villagers in the south of Mosul claiming that they are hosting ISIL militias. On the same day, Iraqi airstrikes targeted a funeral in Kirkuk province causing death of 20 people and injuring dozens others. Mosul's population reached to 1.5 million people, including 600,000 children who are besieged by ISIL militias and suffering from the shortage of food, water, electricity and medical care. ISIL militias monopolize the local hospitals in Mosul and Al-Hemdanyya District to treat only its supporters and members. About 690 families have been evacuated from the Makhmoor District east of Mosul and Al-Hemdanyya District to the Al- Hood camp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-405"><a href="#cite_note-405">[405]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 October, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Governorate" title="Nineveh Governorate">Nineveh Provincial Council</a> stated that ISIL executed 300 civilians and former security members in the village of Moshairefa, north of Mosul. They had been imprisoned and accused of collaborating with the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-406"><a href="#cite_note-406">[406]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i> reported on 3 November that mortar strikes killed five civilians in Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-407"><a href="#cite_note-407">[407]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two roadside bombs struck a convoy of civilians fleeing <a href="/wiki/Hawija" title="Hawija">Hawija</a> on 4 November as the families were being taken to the town of Al-Alam. At least 18 people were killed, a police officer said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-408"><a href="#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 November, the Iraqi War Media Office announced that the <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil_massacre" title="Hamam al-Alil massacre">bodies of estimated 300 people</a> were found in a <a href="/wiki/Mass_grave" title="Mass grave">mass grave</a> at the agriculture college in <a href="/wiki/Hamam_al-Alil" title="Hamam al-Alil">Hamam al-Alil</a>, south of Mosul. Many had been decapitated. Iraqi forces made the discovery after noticing the smell. Abdul Rahman al-Waggaa, a member of the Nineveh provincial council, said ISIL had used the college as "a killing field."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-409"><a href="#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-410"><a href="#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup> The Iraqi War Media Office said there would be an investigation into the murders: "Inside the building of the Faculty of Agriculture there is a new crime: the presence of 100 beheaded bodies of citizens killed by terrorists, and a special team will be sent to inspect this heinous crime," the office said in a statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1107_207-3"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1107-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United Nations reported on 8 November that ISIL had abducted 295 former Iraqi Security Forces members and 1,500 families from Hamam al-Alil, forcing them to retreat with the militants into Mosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411"><a href="#cite_note-411">[411]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 November, it was reported that ISIL killed at least 20 civilians after accusing them of being spies. Five crucified bodies were displayed at a traffic intersection, while others were left hanging from traffic signals and electricity poles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-412"><a href="#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> Civilians who had fled the city in the past few days reported that ISIL was using suicide bombs to attack residents in addition to Iraqi forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-413"><a href="#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> reported on 11 November that ISIL executed 40 civilians in Mosul after accusing them of being spies. One man was killed for defying the ban on mobile phone use. They were shot and their bodies displayed around the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-414"><a href="#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">U.N. Office of Human Rights</a> provided new details that ISIL is using chemical weapons and has stockpiled "large quantities" of ammonia and sulfur. "We can only speculate how they intend to use this," U.N. spokeswoman Ravina Shamdasani said. "We are simply raising the alarm that this is happening, that this is being stockpiled."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-415"><a href="#cite_note-415">[415]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 November, Iraqi forces found two more mass graves near Hamam Alil, containing at least 250 bodies. One of the graves was inside a well. "We believe the well contains more than 200 bodies. ISIS used this mass grave to kill and dump people over the past two years," Iraqi Federal Police Commander Brig. Gen. Faris Radhi Abbas told CNN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-416"><a href="#cite_note-416">[416]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_against_anti-ISIL_forces">Allegations against anti-ISIL forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Allegations against anti-ISIL forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 17 October, the Iraqi central government and KRG authorities launched a military operation to retake Mosul city captured by ISIL in June 2014. In response, ISIL assaulted numbers of buildings and police stations in Kurdish areas, located in the southeast of Mosul, causing death of 100 security force members and civilians. Kurdish authorities are attacking and ejecting Arabs living in Kirkuk into the streets or unsafe areas in order to take revenge on ISIL, which attacked the city on 21 October 2016. On 23 October, the security committee of Kirkuk Governorate has declared that people who live in Kirkuk but were not in camps, have to leave the city or move into a camp for displaced people.</p>
<p>On 23 and 24 October the Kurdish authorities forced 325 families to leave their homes and destroyed about 100 homes in southern Kirkuk. On 25 October, Kurdish bulldozers and excavators demolished dozens of homes, and displaced families from Hawija living in five homes to leave Kirkuk, which is mostly residential. More than 12,000 were expelled by Kurdish forces to live in unsafe conditions in Kirkuk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-417"><a href="#cite_note-417">[417]</a></sup></p>
<p>The presence of several militias with histories of human rights abuses was criticized; <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> called for Shia militias from the Popular Mobilization Forces (PMF) to not enter Mosul, following allegations of severe abuse of Sunni Muslims in anti-ISIL operations in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fallujah_(2016)" title="Battle of Fallujah (2016)">Fallujah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Tikrit" title="Second Battle of Tikrit">Tikrit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Amirli" title="Siege of Amirli">Amirli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-418"><a href="#cite_note-418">[418]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-419"><a href="#cite_note-419">[419]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-420"><a href="#cite_note-420">[420]</a></sup> Iraqi Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">Haider al-Abadi</a> later stated that only the Iraqi army and the Iraqi national police will enter the city itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1016_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1016-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-of1017_421-0"><a href="#cite_note-of1017-421">[421]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 October, <i><a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">International Business Times</a></i> reported that "disturbing and graphic footage posted to social media allegedly shows Iraqi security forces <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torturing</a> and interrogating young children for information about ISIL as they attempt to retake Mosul from the Islamic State terror group."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-422"><a href="#cite_note-422">[422]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 November, video emerged of the Iraqi Special Forces apparently murdering an Iraqi child. The boy, identified as Muhammad Ali Al-Hadidi, was dragged through the desert and shot dead before a tank was driven over him. The men in the video were identified as Shia and yelled sectarian slurs at the child, a Sunni. The video caused outrage on social media, with Arabic speakers using the hashtag #CrushedByATank (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">#السحق_بالدبابة</span>‎‎). The soldiers were wearing the insignia of the Iraqi Special Forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-423"><a href="#cite_note-423">[423]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 19, Iraqi forces summarily executed three civilians who they later claimed were IS suspects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-424"><a href="#cite_note-424">[424]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-425"><a href="#cite_note-425">[425]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Displacements_and_relief_efforts">Displacements and relief efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Displacements and relief efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Italian <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Grandi" title="Filippo Grandi">Filippo Grandi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UN High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, arrived in <a href="/wiki/Erbil" title="Erbil">Erbil</a> on 17 October to meet with Kurdish officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-426"><a href="#cite_note-426">[426]</a></sup> The UN has set up five refugee camps capable of taking up to 45,000 people and has the capability of taking in up to 120,000 if more sites are available for camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1018_427-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1018-427">[427]</a></sup> Dozens of families from Mosul arrived in the <a href="/wiki/Al-Hawl" title="Al-Hawl">Al-Hawl</a> camp in <a href="/wiki/Rojava" title="Rojava">Rojava</a>, Northern Syria, bringing the number of Iraqis in al-Hawl to more than 6,000. On 18 October, more than 2,000 refugees from Mosul were attempting to cross into Syria, according to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Protection_Units" title="People's Protection Units">People's Defense Units</a> (YPG).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudaw1018_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-rudaw1018-104">[104]</a></sup> The UN is attempting to communicate with citizens inside Mosul that they should not flee to the West of the city toward Syria, an area still under ISIL control, but to the camps in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-428"><a href="#cite_note-428">[428]</a></sup></p>
<p>Australia announced it would donate USD$7.5 million in humanitarian aid to the operation, and New Zealand pledged NZ$1 million (USD$718,600).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-429"><a href="#cite_note-429">[429]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) said it had trained 90 Iraqi medics in "mass casualty management" as part of its preparations for the Mosul operation, with a special focus on responding to chemical attacks, AP reported. ISIL has previously used chemical weapons in attacks on Iraqi and coalition forces, and there are fears that it might do so again inside Mosul, where more than a million civilians live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-430"><a href="#cite_note-430">[430]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 November, Kurdish and UN aid workers said more than 40,000 refugees had fled to Kurdistan in the first few weeks of fighting. Ten new refugee camps have been built in the <a href="/wiki/Dohuk_Governorate" title="Dohuk Governorate">Dohuk Governorate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erbil_Governorate" title="Erbil Governorate">Erbil Governorate</a> and in the town of Khazir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-431"><a href="#cite_note-431">[431]</a></sup> According to the United Nations and UNICEF, 22,000 people had been displaced, including more than 9,000 children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-432"><a href="#cite_note-432">[432]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 November, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (UNHCR) stated that 33,996 people had been displaced from the <a href="/wiki/Mosul_District" title="Mosul District">Mosul District</a>. 63 percent of families are missing civil documentation and 21 percent of families are headed by a female.
