The previous 48 hours saw a 53 percent increase in displacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1109_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr1109-44">[44]</a></sup> The following day, WHO announced it had established 82 "rapid response teams" to prepare for possible concerns among civilians fleeing Mosul, including health epidemics such as <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>, and exposure to chemicals and smoke from burning oil wells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-433"><a href="#cite_note-433">[433]</a></sup> A particular concern is potential disease outbreaks among young children who have not been immunized since ISIL took over the city in June 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-434"><a href="#cite_note-434">[434]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than 900 Iraqi civilians have fled to the Al-Hawl refugee camp located in the <a href="/wiki/Rojava" title="Rojava">Rojava</a> region of northeastern <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, while another 700 civilians run away to the <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkish</a>-<a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> borders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-435"><a href="#cite_note-435">[435]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Context">Context</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Context">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_reactions">International reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Jean-Marc_Ayrault" title="Jean-Marc Ayrault">Jean-Marc Ayrault</a>, France's Minister of Foreign Affairs, said on 27 October, "We know that we will face significant challenges and it is our responsibility to face them together, alongside Iraq, while fully respecting its independence and sovereignty."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-436"><a href="#cite_note-436">[436]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a></dt>
<dd>President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> on 17 October said: "We hope that our American partners, and in this case our French partners as well, will act selectively and do everything to minimise — and even better, to rule out — civilian casualties."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-437"><a href="#cite_note-437">[437]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></dt>
<dd>Turkish President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdogan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdogan">Recep Tayyip Erdogan</a> has insisted, as of now without success, on a Turkish role in the battle for Mosul (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mosul_(2016)#Turkey" title="Battle of Mosul (2016)">Turkish involvement</a> below). On 26 October, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Turkey)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Turkey)">Turkish FM</a> <a href="/wiki/Mevl%C3%BCt_%C3%87avu%C5%9Fo%C4%9Flu" title="Mevlüt Çavuşoğlu">Mevlüt Çavuşoğlu</a> said "Fighting ISIL is necessary, but the process after ISIL must be planned carefully."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-438"><a href="#cite_note-438">[438]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></dt>
<dd>Then-President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> said on 18 October, "Mosul will be a difficult fight and there will be advances and setbacks. I am confident, just as ISIL has been defeated in communities across Iraq, ISIL will be defeated in Mosul as well, and that will be another step toward their ultimate destruction." then-Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/Ash_Carter" title="Ash Carter">Ash Carter</a> on 16 October said in a statement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-439"><a href="#cite_note-439">[439]</a></sup> "This is a decisive moment in the campaign to deliver ISIL a lasting defeat."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-440"><a href="#cite_note-440">[440]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage_and_social_media">Media coverage and social media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media coverage and social media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several media outlets including <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> live streamed the first day's battle on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, a first in war coverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-441"><a href="#cite_note-441">[441]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-442"><a href="#cite_note-442">[442]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-443"><a href="#cite_note-443">[443]</a></sup> Additional live video feeds were available on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and the streaming app <a href="/wiki/Periscope_(app)" title="Periscope (app)">Periscope</a>. Iraqi and Kurdish officials are also joining in on social media using the <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtag</a> #FreeMosul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-444"><a href="#cite_note-444">[444]</a></sup> Brendan Gauthier, assistant editor of <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i>, noted that given ISIL's slick campaigns on social media, "It's only appropriate then that the Iraqi military’s effort to reclaim Mosul from the PR machine turned extremist group be live-streamed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-445"><a href="#cite_note-445">[445]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 October, several Iraqi media outlets established the National Media Alliance to support journalists reporting on the battle. The groups include both government-run and private media, including <a href="/wiki/Al_Iraqiya" title="Al Iraqiya">Al Iraqiya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Sumaria" title="Al Sumaria">Al Sumaria</a>. The alliance provides technical and journalistic services, including a joint operations newsroom. It was formed to counter ISIL propaganda and foster cooperation among the various media groups in order to reduce chaos and improve safety. Journalist Walid al-Tai told <a href="/wiki/Al-Monitor" title="Al-Monitor">Al-Monitor</a>, "One of the reasons behind the establishment of the alliance is to avoid any chaotic media coverage of the battle as every media and military institution is sending its correspondents to battlefronts. This leads to conflict in the coverage of the fighting and a greater number of casualties among journalists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-446"><a href="#cite_note-446">[446]</a></sup></p>
<p>Journalist Mustafa Habib reported that Iraqi citizens are coordinating efforts on Facebook and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> to counter ISIL propaganda, such as fake photos and videos, that may be used to intimidate locals in Mosul. A communications department of a Shia militia also announced it would be contributing to a social media campaign, and that 500 Iraqi journalists were <a href="/wiki/Embedded_journalism" title="Embedded journalism">embedded</a> with the militias surrounding Mosul to report updates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-447"><a href="#cite_note-447">[447]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 October 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Robin_Wright_(author)" title="Robin Wright (author)">Robin Wright</a> interviewed the anonymous self-described historian <i><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Eye" title="Mosul Eye">Mosul Eye</a></i>, a purported Mosuli who has blogged from the city about life in Mosul under ISIL despite death threats from the group. Responding to Wright's questions, <i>Mosul Eye</i> estimated the size and make-up of ISIL's force in Mosul, hopes for the future ("gain back power over the city" with help of "an international trusteeship to protect Mosul"), and the level of support for ISIL inside Mosul ("There is no support for ISIL in Mosul. They are left only with weapons that they will use to kill themselves once the liberating forces make the decision to raid the city.").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkish_involvement"><span id="Turkey"></span> Turkish involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Mosul_(2016%E2%80%9317)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Turkish involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The involvement of Turkey in the operation has considerably strained its relations with Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj1023_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-aj1023-5">[5]</a></sup> Turkey has 1,500 to 2,000 soldiers in Iraq,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MathieuKodmani1016_448-0"><a href="#cite_note-MathieuKodmani1016-448">[448]</a></sup> including 500 Turkish soldiers deployed to a base near <a href="/wiki/Bashiqa" title="Bashiqa">Bashiqa</a>, where they trained 1,500 Iraqi Sunni volunteers, mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen" title="Iraqi Turkmen">Turkmens</a>, and Arabs to recapture Mosul from ISIL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-449"><a href="#cite_note-449">[449]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-450"><a href="#cite_note-450">[450]</a></sup> Turkey's participation is against the wishes of the Iraqi government, which has said the Turks are violating Iraq's sovereignty. Turkey has refused to withdraw its forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj1023_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-aj1023-5">[5]</a></sup> Turkish President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdogan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdogan">Recep Tayyip Erdogan</a> told the Turkish parliament on 1 October, "We will play a role in the Mosul liberation operation and no one can prevent us from participating,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-451"><a href="#cite_note-451">[451]</a></sup> and said their presence was to ensure that Mosul did not fall to Kurdish or Shia control and become a threat to Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-452"><a href="#cite_note-452">[452]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-453"><a href="#cite_note-453">[453]</a></sup> Turkey's presence was criticized by Kurds in northern Iraq,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-454"><a href="#cite_note-454">[454]</a></sup> and thousands of protestors demonstrated at the Turkish Embassy in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> on 18 October, demanding Turkish forces withdraw from Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-455"><a href="#cite_note-455">[455]</a></sup> The United States has reportedly attempted to persuade Iraq to cooperate with Turkey on the Mosul offensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-456"><a href="#cite_note-456">[456]</a></sup> Al-Abadi declined the offer of Turkish assistance, saying, "I know that the Turks want to participate. We tell them thank you, this is something the Iraqis will handle and the Iraqis will liberate Mosul and the rest of the territories."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-457"><a href="#cite_note-457">[457]</a></sup> However, on 23 October, Turkish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Binali_Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1r%C4%B1m" title="Binali Yıldırım">Binali Yıldırım</a> announced Turkish troops had fired on ISIL positions near Mosul after requests for assistance from the Peshmerga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj1023_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-aj1023-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The situation between Turkey and Iraq escalated on 1 November, the day Iraqi forces entered Mosul. Turkey announced it was sending tanks and artillery from Ankara to <a href="/wiki/Silopi" title="Silopi">Silopi</a> near the Iraqi border. Turkey's Minister of Defense <a href="/wiki/Fikri_I%C5%9F%C4%B1k" title="Fikri Işık">Fikri Işık</a> said the deployment was a move to "prepare for "important developments" in the region and be ready for any possible scenario" and stated that "further action can be taken if Turkey's red lines are crossed" warning Shi'ite militias and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PKK" title="PKK">PKK</a> not to "terrorize" and take hold of <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Iraqi Turkmen</a>-majority regions in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-458"><a href="#cite_note-458">[458]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-459"><a href="#cite_note-459">[459]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-460"><a href="#cite_note-460">[460]</a></sup> Prime Minister Al-Abadi warned Turkey not to "invade" Iraq, predicting war if they did. Al-Abadi, addressing journalists in Baghdad, said, "We warn Turkey if they want to enter Iraq, they will end up becoming fragmented... We do not want to fight Turkey. We do not want a confrontation with Turkey. God forbid, even if we engage in war with them, the Turks will pay a heavy price. They will be damaged. Yes, we too will be damaged, but whenever a country fights a neighboring country, there will be no winner, both will end up losing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-461"><a href="#cite_note-461">[461]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 November, Iraq rejected Turkey’s proposal to continue running the Bashiqa military camp, no matter if it were formally transferred under the auspices of the coalition forces, and suggested that Turkey hand over control of the camp to Iraq’s central government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-462"><a href="#cite_note-462">[462]</a></sup></p>
